# Pre-UAT Deep Diagnostic — Resume-After-Interruption  
**Mode:** Logs + State + Code Triangulation (use all together)

---

## 🎯 Role
You are a **senior reliability engineer**. Investigate, troubleshoot, and analyze the system’s **resume-after-interruption** behavior for **clearance-king**. **Do not design new mechanisms or architectures.** Assume clamps/guards already exist (for denominators and numerators) and must be **verified and minimally corrected** to meet the intended contracts.

> **Think privately first.** Do your step-by-step analysis on a hidden scratchpad. In the final output, present **only** the requested report sections and evidence.

---

## 🔐 Scope Guarantees (treat as constraints)
- **Denominator freeze:** Keys like *_products_needing_* freeze once set and **must not change** across runs.  
- **Numerator monotonicity & clamping:** Keys like *_products_completed **never regress** and are **≤** their frozen denominators.  
- **PCI monotonicity:** The **Persistent Category Index (PCI)** **never decreases** across runs.  
- **Sequence:** **Freeze → Mark → Resume** governs resumption.  
- **Phase-aware routing:** Distinct **supplier** vs **amazon_analysis** phases; routing on restart must honor persisted phase.  
- **Atomic persistence:** All writes go through **WindowsSaveGuardian**.  
- **Empty-category semantics:** If denominator = 0 ⇒ **immediate completion; PCI advances; product index resets only for that category**.

Your job: **Verify** these are implemented, identify **malfunctions/partials**, and propose **precise, minimal corrections** to existing clamps/guards.

---

**A) Logs (two consecutive runs; state cleared before Run #1)**

---

## 🧭 Contracts to Validate (what “correct” looks like)
1. **Phase-aware resumption:** On restart, read persisted {phase, cat_idx, prod_idx} and **route directly** into that phase’s loop (**supplier** or **amazon_analysis**) **without recomputing pointers**.  
2. **Monotonic pointers:**  
   - **PCI** never decreases.  
   - **Product indices** (supplier & Amazon) never decrease and are clamped to their frozen denominators.  
3. **Frozen denominators:** Once frozen per category, denominators **remain unchanged** across runs (unless an explicit, documented override is enabled).  
4. **Empty categories:** denominator = 0 ⇒ **mark complete**, **advance PCI**, and **reset product index for that category only**.  
5. **Atomicity & observability:** Every increment is **atomically saved**; logs must emit **authoritative resume decisions** after freeze/rehydration is known.

---

## 🧲 What to Extract (minimum fields & events)

### From JSON (both snapshots)
Capture and compare at least:
- system_progression.current_phase  
- system_progression.persistent_category_index (PCI)  
- system_progression.current_category_url  
- system_progression.frozen_totals_committed *(or equivalent)*  
- supplier_products_needing_extraction, supplier_products_completed  
- amazon_products_needing_analysis, amazon_products_completed  
- Any per-category counters/flags that drive completion/advance.

### From Logs (both runs)
Timeline and parse:
- **Authoritative resume** lines (startup/dispatch/resume breadcrumbs)  
- **Phase routing** decisions (supplier vs Amazon)  
- **Denominator freeze/mark** events and any “change blocked/allowed” notes  
- **Progress increments & clamps** (supplier & Amazon)  
- **Category completion** calls and URL match/mismatch notes  
- **Atomic save** confirmations and any **regression/overwrite warnings**

### From Code (current snapshot)
Locate exact clamp/guard logic and where it’s invoked:
- Denominator **freeze** + “**no recompute on resume**” guard  
- Numerator **clamp**: new_done = max(old_done, incoming_done) and new_done ≤ denom  
- **PCI monotonic** rule (no backslide)  
- **Overflow** clamps (indices ≤ denominators)  
- Where **phase** is **loaded** vs **(re)set/overwritten**  
- Where **resume pointer** is built/consumed (persisted values vs derived from transient queues)  
- **Empty category** handling & **URL normalization** (if required)  
- All writes via **WindowsSaveGuardian**

> **Citation style:** For every claim, cite **at least two** of {**[LOG]**, **[JSON]**, **[CODE]**}. Prefer **three**. Include file path + line/time hint if available.

---

## 🧪 Analysis Procedure (do not skip steps)

1. **Two-Run Timeline**  
   Build a stepwise narrative for each run: **startup → freeze/rehydration → routing → processing → completion → final save**.  
   - At each step, record **phase, PCI, denominators, product counters** using concrete values from **logs** and matching values from **JSON**.

2. **Clamp/Guard Map (in Code)**  
   Point to line-level locations implementing:  
   a) **Denominator freeze** + “no recompute on resume” guard  
   b) **Numerator clamp** (non-regression, ≤ denom)  
   c) **PCI monotonic** rule  
   d) **Overflow** clamps  
   Confirm invocation in both runs via **logs + state deltas**.

3. **Phase & Resume Pointer Flow**  
   Show where **phase** is loaded and where it might be **defaulted/overwritten**.  
   Explain how **starting product index** (supplier/Amazon) is computed on resume: **persisted *_completed (correct)** vs **freshly rebuilt lists (incorrect)**.  
   If lists are rebuilt, confirm whether existing clamps **correct back to the persisted high-water mark**.

4. **Empty Category & URL Normalization**  
   Verify denominator = 0 code path: **immediate completion**, **PCI++**, **category-local product index reset**.  
   If URL matching is involved, verify **normalization at both write & check sites** and show any mismatches evidenced in logs/JSON.

5. **Cross-Run Invariant Matrix**  
   Build a table comparing **Run #1 end → Run #2 start → Run #2 end** for: **phase, PCI, denominators, numerators (supplier + Amazon)**.  
   Mark each cell **✅ met**, **⚠️ partial (guard corrected)**, or **❌ violated**.

6. **Root Causes (multi-source proof)**  
   For each failure/partial, provide:  
   - **[CODE]** file:line snippet of the clamp/guard or the missing check  
   - **[LOG]** line(s) showing behavior  
   - **[JSON]** fields/values confirming state evolution

7. **Suggested Fixes (minimal corrections only)**  
   Adjust or **relocate existing clamps/guards** so they run at the **correct time** and **use persisted sources of truth**.  
   If a guard exists but is bypassed by ordering, recommend the **smallest change** (call sequence, condition tweak, or log placement).  
   Prefer **normalization at both write and check sites** for URL equality.  
   Provide **pseudo-diffs** (tiny deltas; **no refactors**; **no new mechanisms**).

8. **Acceptance Tests (targeted)**  
   Author **test recipes** (not code) proving each contract with **two-run scenarios**:  
   - Mid-supplier, mid-Amazon, empty category, last category, repeated restart.  
   Each test must assert behavior using **persisted values** and show expected **logs/JSON** artifacts.

---

## 📤 Output Format (strict)
Produce **one** “Comprehensive Diagnostic Report” with the sections below **in order**. Use concise bullets, tables, and embedded evidence.

1) **System Map (Resume Surfaces)**  
   Numbered steps of **state load**, **clamp points**, **phase routing**, and **save sites** — include **file:line** references.

2) **Evidence Table (Triangulated)**  
   **Each row = one observed behavior** (resume pointer, denom freeze, product index, PCI, completion).  
   **Columns:** *Log snippet(s) → JSON field(s) → Code snippet(line#) → Verdict (Met/Partial/Broken)*.

3) **Issue Catalog**  
   For each issue: **Symptom, Scope, Frequency, Impact, Exact code locations, Triggering log patterns**.

4) **Root Causes (with Multi-Source Proof)**  
   Minimum **1 code snippet + 1 log line + 1 JSON field** per cause.

5) **Suggested Fixes (Minimal Corrections)**  
   Smallest viable changes to **existing** clamps/guards, with **pseudo-diffs** and **ordering** notes (**Freeze → Mark → Resume**).

6) **Repro Steps & Acceptance Checks**  
   Step-by-step recipes per scenario; expected **logs/JSON**; how clamps/guards prove correctness.

7) **Prioritization**  
   **P0** (breaks correctness), **P1** (violates contracts but guarded), **P2** (observability/docs).

8) **Open Questions**  
   Missing files, ambiguities, or assumptions made.

> **Hard requirements:**  
> - **Every claim cites ≥2 sources** from {**[LOG]**, **[JSON]**, **[CODE]**}; prefer **3**.  
> - **No new mechanisms. No code edits in this run.** Only design-level or ordering corrections to **existing** clamps/guards.  
> - Be explicit about **where** each clamp/guard **fires** and **why that ordering is required**.

---

## 🧯 Guardrails
- **Do not** propose new resume structures or persistence layers.  
- **Do not** refactor broadly; stick to **tiny deltas**.  
- Keep **Freeze → Mark → Resume** sequencing explicit.

---

## ✍️ Tiny Before/After Example (illustrative)
- **Before:** “Empty category ⇒ complete.”  
- **After:** “If denominator == 0, immediately **mark category complete**, **advance PCI by 1**, and **reset the product index only for that category**; persist via **WindowsSaveGuardian** and log the authoritative resume pointer.”

5) Suggested Fixes (Minimal Corrections)

F-1 (P0): Do not overwrite persisted phase
Where: utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py :: initialize_category_processing()
Delta (pseudo-diff):

- base = {
-   "current_phase": "supplier",
-   "current_category_url": normalized_category_url,
-   "original_category_url": category_url,
-   "total_categories": total_categories,
- }
- sp.update(base)
+ # Preserve persisted phase; only set default if missing
+ sp.setdefault("current_phase", "supplier")
+ sp["current_category_url"] = normalized_category_url
+ sp["original_category_url"] = category_url
+ sp["total_categories"] = total_categories

  2. ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS

  Root Cause #1: Stateful Initialization Overwrites Loaded State

  Pattern: Load state → Process → Overwrite → UseShould Be: Load state → Preserve → Process → Use

  Why It Happens:
  # initialize_category_processing() creates a "base" dict:
  base = {
      "current_phase": "supplier",  # ← Hardcoded value
      ...
  }
  sp.update(base)  # ← Overwrites ALL keys in base, including loaded phase

  Fix: Conditional initialization (only set if missing)

  ---
  Root Cause #2: File-Based State Not Used for Resume Calculations

  Pattern: Calculate from memory counters (unreliable)Should Be: Calculate from file state (reliable)

  Why It Happens:
  - System has filtering logic that counts files (lines 5400-5500)
  - But resume pointer calculation doesn't use those counts
  - Instead, system starts from 0 or uses unreliable memory counters

  Fix: Use file counts to calculate resume position

  ---
  Root Cause #3: Phase Detection Ignores Persisted State

  Pattern: Recalculate phase from filesShould Be: Trust persisted phase first, fallback to calculation

  Why It Happens:

  if supplier_cache_count == 0:
      current_phase = "SUPPLIER_EXTRACTION"
  # But never checks: sp.get("current_phase")

  Fix: Read persisted phase first, only calculate if missing

  FIX #2: Phase-Aware Resume Routing

  Priority: 🔴 P0 CRITICALFile: tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.pyLines: 2140-2180 (new function + routing logic)Estimated Effort: 2 hours

  NEW FUNCTION TO ADD:
  def calculate_file_based_resume_position(self, category_url: str) -> dict:
      """
      Calculate resume position from actual file state (not memory counters).

      Returns:
          {
              "persisted_phase": str,              # From system_progression
              "resume_product_index": int,         # Start here (1-based)
              "total_products": int,               # Frozen denominator
              "linking_map_count": int,            # Products in linking map
              "cache_count": int,                  # Products in supplier cache
              "products_remaining": int,           # Need processing
              "filter_invariant_holds": bool       # Validation check
          }
      """
      sp = self.state_manager.state_data.get("system_progression", {})

      # STEP 1: Get frozen denominator (single source of truth)
      frozen_denominators = sp.get("frozen_category_denominators", {})
      total_products = frozen_denominators.get(category_url, 0)

      # STEP 2: Count linking map entries (Amazon completed)
      linking_map_path = self.fba_reports_manager.get_linking_map_path(self.supplier_name)
      linking_map = self._load_json_safe(linking_map_path, {})

      # Count only successful matches (exclude match_method="none")
      linking_map_count = len([
          k for k, v in linking_map.items()
          if isinstance(v, dict) and v.get("match_method") != "none"
      ])

      # STEP 3: Count supplier cache entries (Supplier completed)
      cache_path = os.path.join(
          self.base_output_path,
          "cached_products",
          f"{self.supplier_name}_products_cache.json"
      )
      supplier_cache = self._load_json_safe(cache_path, [])
      cache_count = len(supplier_cache)

      # STEP 4: Get persisted phase (AUTHORITY)
      persisted_phase = sp.get("current_phase", "supplier")

      # STEP 5: Calculate resume position based on phase
      if persisted_phase == "amazon_analysis":
          # Resume after last linking map entry
          resume_index = linking_map_count + 1
          products_remaining = total_products - linking_map_count

      else:  # supplier phase
          # Resume after last cache entry + linking map entries
          # (linking map products were skipped by EAN filter)
          resume_index = cache_count + linking_map_count + 1
          products_remaining = total_products - cache_count - linking_map_count

      # STEP 6: Validate filter invariant
      filter_invariant_holds = (
          total_products == linking_map_count + cache_count + products_remaining
      )

      return {
          "persisted_phase": persisted_phase,
          "resume_product_index": resume_index,
          "total_products": total_products,
          "linking_map_count": linking_map_count,
          "cache_count": cache_count,
          "products_remaining": products_remaining,
          "filter_invariant_holds": filter_invariant_holds
      }

  ROUTING LOGIC TO ADD (after loading state, before processing):
  # File: tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py
  # Location: After line 2180 (after state loading)

  # Calculate resume position from files
  resume_position = self.calculate_file_based_resume_position(category_url)

  # Log evidence
  self.log.info(
      f"📋 FILE-BASED RESUME CALCULATION:\n"
      f"  Persisted Phase: {resume_position['persisted_phase']}\n"
      f"  Resume from product: {resume_position['resume_product_index']}\n"
      f"  Total products: {resume_position['total_products']}\n"
      f"  Evidence:\n"
      f"    - Linking map: {resume_position['linking_map_count']} complete\n"
      f"    - Supplier cache: {resume_position['cache_count']} cached\n"
      f"    - Products remaining: {resume_position['products_remaining']}\n"
      f"    - Filter invariant: {'✅ PASS' if resume_position['filter_invariant_holds'] else '❌ FAIL'}"
  )

  # Validate filter invariant
  if not resume_position['filter_invariant_holds']:
      self.log.error(
          f"🚨 FILTER INVARIANT VIOLATION: "
          f"{resume_position['total_products']} != "
          f"{resume_position['linking_map_count']} + "
          f"{resume_position['cache_count']} + "
          f"{resume_position['products_remaining']}"
      )

  # Route based on persisted phase (NOT file counts!)
  if resume_position['persisted_phase'] == "amazon_analysis":
      self.log.info(f"🎯 RESUMING IN AMAZON PHASE (from product {resume_position['resume_product_index']})")
      # Skip directly to Amazon loop
      # (supplier phase is complete - current_phase says so!)

  else:
      self.log.info(f"🎯 RESUMING IN SUPPLIER PHASE (from product {resume_position['resume_product_index']})")
      # Process supplier phase

  Why This Works:
  - ✅ Reads persisted phase (AUTHORITY)
  - ✅ Calculates resume position from files (RELIABLE)
  - ✅ Validates filter invariant (SAFETY)
  - ✅ Routes based on phase (CORRECT)

  FIX #3: EAN-First Linking Map Filtering (Your Enhancement)

  Priority: 🟢 P2 OPTIMIZATION (Reduces Duplicate Work)File: tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.pyLines: 5380-5440Estimated Effort: 1 hour

  EXACT CODE (as you provided):
  # Filter URLs against linking map (SKIP_ENTIRELY)
  skip_entirely_urls = []
  remaining_after_linking_map = []

  for url in urls_for_manifest:
      # 🚨 RC-3 FIX: Use canonical normalization for consistent filtering
      normalized_url = normalize_url(url)

      # Get EAN from product cache if available for linking map check
      product_ean = None
      if hasattr(self, "product_cache_url_index"):
          p_for_ean = self.product_cache_url_index.get(normalized_url)
          if p_for_ean:
              product_ean = p_for_ean.get("ean")

      # 🚨 NEW: EAN-first linking map check (primary skip condition)
      skip_due_to_linking_map = False

      # Primary check: EAN-based filtering (if EAN available)
      if product_ean and product_ean in processed_eans:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 EAN-based linking map skip: {url} (EAN: {product_ean})")

      # Secondary check: URL-based filtering (fallback)
      elif normalized_url in processed_urls:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 URL-based linking map skip: {url}")

      if not skip_due_to_linking_map:
          remaining_after_linking_map.append(url)

  Why This Works:
  - ✅ EAN-first matching (more reliable than URL)
  - ✅ URL fallback (backward compatibility)
  - ✅ Prevents duplicate supplier extractions
  - ✅ Cleaner file state (accurate cache counts)

Read from state at startup and used to pick a starting pointer.
(Workflow reads resume_phase = sp["current_phase"] and logs a resumption point.)

Then it gets overwritten to "supplier" during category init and later recomputed from file counts in workflow routing.

Route based on the persisted phase (not the counts).

“Start indexes for completed/processed must be calculated from files (product cache / linking map).

amazon_start = max(saved_amazon_completed, linking_map_count)

Then ignore the saved counters for control flow; use the file-derived start in the loops.

Keep writing the counters if you want the banner to show something, but make those writes non-destructive: saved = max(saved, in_run_cursor) so they never lower a previously higher value.

Expected behavior after change

Restarts pick up where files say you are.

If some items slipped through the two-step filter (duplicate EAN across URLs, etc.), you might reprocess a few—acceptable by your rule—but you never “lose place”.

4) Denominators (*_products_needing_*)
Current code (what it does now)

Maintains per-category counters and a “frozen” flag; supplier denom was stable (64), Amazon drifted (42 → 41) across your two runs.

C) The clamp/guard question you raised
“There was never regression. Seeing 7 then 4 isn’t regression; those are per-run counts.”

Current semantics in code: the *_completed fields are stored in state and then read on restart to compute the resume pointer. Under that meaning, 7 → 4 in state is a regression in the saved high-water mark, even if your session output advanced. That’s why the next run started earlier than it should.

With your new rule (file-driven start): we can stop relying on the saved counters for control flow. They can still be written for display, but we should ensure they never lower previously saved values (so banners don’t flicker backwards).
That’s the reason I suggested a tiny max(saved, cursor)—not to change your file-driven resume, but to avoid confusing state if the banner continues to report from state.

Bottom line:

If we entirely ignore state counters for resumption and only use file counts, you can remove the monotonic clamps from a correctness standpoint.

I still recommend keeping max(saved, cursor) on writes to avoid cosmetic backward numbers in logs/UI—even if control flow ignores them. It’s a 2-line, zero-risk guard.

  def initialize_category_processing(
      self, category_index: int, category_url: str, total_categories: int
  ):
      """
      Initialize tracking for a new category while preserving loaded state.

      CRITICAL FIXES:
      1. Preserves loaded current_phase (doesn't overwrite to "supplier")
      2. Explicitly writes PCI when blocking regression
      3. Updates ONLY category context fields (no dict with phase/PCI)
      """
      from utils.normalization import normalize_url
      normalized_category_url = normalize_url(category_url)

      sp = self.state_data.setdefault("system_progression", {})

      # ✅ FIX #1: PCI Preservation with Explicit Write
      current_pci = sp.get("persistent_category_index")

      if current_pci is None:
          # Fresh start: Set initial PCI
          sp["persistent_category_index"] = int(category_index)
          log.info(f"🆕 INITIAL PCI: Set to {category_index}")
      else:
          incoming = int(category_index)
          current = int(current_pci)

          if incoming < current:
              # ✅ CRITICAL: Explicitly preserve current PCI!
              sp["persistent_category_index"] = current
              log.warning(
                  f"🔒 REGRESSION BLOCKED: {current} → {incoming} "
                  f"(explicitly preserved PCI={current})"
              )
          elif incoming > current:
              # Forward advancement
              sp["persistent_category_index"] = incoming
              log.info(f"✅ PCI ADVANCED: {current} → {incoming}")
          else:
              # incoming == current, no change
              log.debug(f"🔍 PCI UNCHANGED: {current}")

      # ✅ FIX #2: Phase Preservation (Conditional Initialization)
      current_phase = sp.get("current_phase")

      if not current_phase:
          # Fresh start: Set default phase
          sp["current_phase"] = "supplier"
          log.info("🆕 INITIAL PHASE: Set to 'supplier'")
      else:
          # Resume: Preserve loaded phase
          log.info(f"✅ PHASE PRESERVED: '{current_phase}' (loaded from state)")

      # ✅ FIX #3: Update ONLY Category Context (Not Phase/PCI)
      # Remove base dict and sp.update() - use individual assignments
      sp["current_category_url"] = normalized_category_url
      sp["original_category_url"] = category_url
      sp["total_categories"] = total_categories

      # Resumption detection logic (unchanged)
      frozen_now = bool(sp.get("category_denominator_frozen"))
      active_idx = int(sp.get("persistent_category_index", 1))
      active_category = (category_index == active_idx)
      is_resumption = active_category or frozen_now

      if is_resumption:
          log.info(
              f"🔄 RESUMPTION: Preserving counters "
              f"(active={active_category}, frozen={frozen_now}) "
              f"for {normalized_category_url}"
          )
      else:
          log.info(f"🆕 NEW CATEGORY: {normalized_category_url}")

      # Add verification logging
      log.info(
          f"📋 CATEGORY INIT COMPLETE:\n"
          f"  PCI: {sp.get('persistent_category_index')}\n"
          f"  Phase: {sp.get('current_phase')}\n"
          f"  Category URL: {normalized_category_url}"
      )

      self.save_state_atomic("category-init")

  # ✅ USER REQUIREMENT: EAN-first linking map filtering
  # Products in linking map are skipped completely (no supplier extraction)

  skip_entirely_urls = []
  remaining_after_linking_map = []

  for url in urls_for_manifest:
      # Canonical normalization
      normalized_url = normalize_url(url)

      # Get EAN from product cache if available
      product_ean = None
      if hasattr(self, "product_cache_url_index"):
          p_for_ean = self.product_cache_url_index.get(normalized_url)
          if p_for_ean:
              product_ean = p_for_ean.get("ean")

      # ✅ EAN-first linking map check (primary skip condition)
      skip_due_to_linking_map = False

      # PRIMARY CHECK: EAN-based filtering (if EAN available)
      if product_ean and product_ean in processed_eans:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 EAN-based linking map skip: {url} (EAN: {product_ean})")

      # SECONDARY CHECK: URL-based filtering (fallback)
      elif normalized_url in processed_urls:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 URL-based linking map skip: {url}")

      # Product not in linking map - needs processing
      if not skip_due_to_linking_map:
          remaining_after_linking_map.append(url)

  # Log filter results
  self.log.info(
      f"📊 LINKING MAP FILTER RESULTS:\n"
      f"  Total URLs: {len(urls_for_manifest)}\n"
      f"  Skipped (in linking map): {len(skip_entirely_urls)}\n"
      f"  Remaining for processing: {len(remaining_after_linking_map)}"
  )

  def initialize_category_processing(
      self, category_index: int, category_url: str, total_categories: int
  ):
      """
      Initialize tracking for a new category while preserving loaded state.

      CRITICAL FIXES:
      1. Preserves loaded current_phase (doesn't overwrite to "supplier")
      2. Explicitly writes PCI when blocking regression
      3. Updates ONLY category context fields (no dict with phase/PCI)
      """
      from utils.normalization import normalize_url
      normalized_category_url = normalize_url(category_url)

      sp = self.state_data.setdefault("system_progression", {})

      # ✅ FIX #1: PCI Preservation with Explicit Write
      current_pci = sp.get("persistent_category_index")

      if current_pci is None:
          # Fresh start: Set initial PCI
          sp["persistent_category_index"] = int(category_index)
          log.info(f"🆕 INITIAL PCI: Set to {category_index}")
      else:
          incoming = int(category_index)
          current = int(current_pci)

          if incoming < current:
              # ✅ CRITICAL: Explicitly preserve current PCI!
              sp["persistent_category_index"] = current
              log.warning(
                  f"🔒 REGRESSION BLOCKED: {current} → {incoming} "
                  f"(explicitly preserved PCI={current})"
              )
          elif incoming > current:
              # Forward advancement
              sp["persistent_category_index"] = incoming
              log.info(f"✅ PCI ADVANCED: {current} → {incoming}")
          else:
              # incoming == current, no change
              log.debug(f"🔍 PCI UNCHANGED: {current}")

      # ✅ FIX #2: Phase Preservation (Conditional Initialization)
      current_phase = sp.get("current_phase")

      if not current_phase:
          # Fresh start: Set default phase
          sp["current_phase"] = "supplier"
          log.info("🆕 INITIAL PHASE: Set to 'supplier'")
      else:
          # Resume: Preserve loaded phase
          log.info(f"✅ PHASE PRESERVED: '{current_phase}' (loaded from state)")

      # ✅ FIX #3: Update ONLY Category Context (Not Phase/PCI)
      # Remove base dict and sp.update() - use individual assignments
      sp["current_category_url"] = normalized_category_url
      sp["original_category_url"] = category_url
      sp["total_categories"] = total_categories

      # Resumption detection logic (unchanged)
      frozen_now = bool(sp.get("category_denominator_frozen"))
      active_idx = int(sp.get("persistent_category_index", 1))
      active_category = (category_index == active_idx)
      is_resumption = active_category or frozen_now

      if is_resumption:
          log.info(
              f"🔄 RESUMPTION: Preserving counters "
              f"(active={active_category}, frozen={frozen_now}) "
              f"for {normalized_category_url}"
          )
      else:
          log.info(f"🆕 NEW CATEGORY: {normalized_category_url}")

      # Add verification logging
      log.info(
          f"📋 CATEGORY INIT COMPLETE:\n"
          f"  PCI: {sp.get('persistent_category_index')}\n"
          f"  Phase: {sp.get('current_phase')}\n"
          f"  Category URL: {normalized_category_url}"
      )

      self.save_state_atomic("category-init")

  FIXED CODE (User's Exact Specification):

  # ✅ USER REQUIREMENT: EAN-first linking map filtering
  # Products in linking map are skipped completely (no supplier extraction)

  skip_entirely_urls = []
  remaining_after_linking_map = []

  for url in urls_for_manifest:
      # Canonical normalization
      normalized_url = normalize_url(url)

      # Get EAN from product cache if available
      product_ean = None
      if hasattr(self, "product_cache_url_index"):
          p_for_ean = self.product_cache_url_index.get(normalized_url)
          if p_for_ean:
              product_ean = p_for_ean.get("ean")

      # ✅ EAN-first linking map check (primary skip condition)
      skip_due_to_linking_map = False

      # PRIMARY CHECK: EAN-based filtering (if EAN available)
      if product_ean and product_ean in processed_eans:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 EAN-based linking map skip: {url} (EAN: {product_ean})")

      # SECONDARY CHECK: URL-based filtering (fallback)
      elif normalized_url in processed_urls:
          skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
          skip_due_to_linking_map = True
          self.log.debug(f"🔗 URL-based linking map skip: {url}")

      # Product not in linking map - needs processing
      if not skip_due_to_linking_map:
          remaining_after_linking_map.append(url)

  # Log filter results
  self.log.info(
      f"📊 LINKING MAP FILTER RESULTS:\n"
      f"  Total URLs: {len(urls_for_manifest)}\n"
      f"  Skipped (in linking map): {len(skip_entirely_urls)}\n"
      f"  Remaining for processing: {len(remaining_after_linking_map)}"
  )

  # ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
  # RESUME POSITION CALCULATION (File-Based, User Requirement)
  # ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

  # Get persisted phase (AUTHORITY for resume routing)
  sp = self.state_manager.state_data.get("system_progression", {})
  persisted_phase = sp.get("current_phase", "supplier")

  # Calculate counts from filter outputs (already computed above)
  in_count = len(urls_for_manifest)          # Total extracted URLs
  skip_count = len(skip_entirely_urls)       # In linking map (skip)
  cached_count = len(cached_keys)            # In cache (cached)
  full_count = len(needs_full_extraction_urls)  # Need full extraction

  # ✅ VALIDATION: Filter invariant check
  filter_invariant_holds = (in_count == skip_count + cached_count + full_count)

  if not filter_invariant_holds:
      self.log.error(
          f"🚨 FILTER INVARIANT VIOLATION:\n"
          f"  in={in_count} != skip={skip_count} + cached={cached_count} + full={full_count}\n"
          f"  Difference: {in_count - (skip_count + cached_count + full_count)}"
      )
  else:
      self.log.info(
          f"✅ FILTER INVARIANT VALIDATED:\n"
          f"  in={in_count} == skip={skip_count} + cached={cached_count} + full={full_count}"
      )

  # ✅ USER REQUIREMENT: Set denominators from filter (both phases use same)
  sp["supplier_products_needing_extraction"] = in_count
  sp["amazon_products_needing_analysis"] = in_count

  # ✅ FROZEN DENOMINATOR: Store for validation (non-mutating)
  frozen_denominators = sp.setdefault("frozen_category_denominators", {})
  category_url_normalized = normalize_url(category_url)

  if category_url_normalized not in frozen_denominators:
      # First time seeing this category - freeze
      frozen_denominators[category_url_normalized] = in_count
      self.log.info(f"🔒 FROZEN DENOMINATOR: {category_url_normalized} = {in_count}")
  else:
      # Validation: Check if denominator changed
      frozen_value = frozen_denominators[category_url_normalized]
      if frozen_value != in_count:
          self.log.warning(
              f"⚠️ DENOMINATOR DRIFT DETECTED:\n"
              f"  Category: {category_url_normalized}\n"
              f"  Frozen: {frozen_value}\n"
              f"  Current: {in_count}\n"
              f"  Using current value (website may have changed)"
          )

  # ✅ RESUME START CALCULATION (Phase-Aware)
  if persisted_phase == "amazon_analysis":
      # Amazon phase: Resume after last linking map entry
      resume_start_index = skip_count + 1
      worklist_type = "amazon_only"
      worklist = needs_amazon_only_urls

      self.log.info(
          f"🎯 RESUMING IN AMAZON PHASE:\n"
          f"  Resume from product: {resume_start_index} (after {skip_count} in linking map)\n"
          f"  Products to process: {len(worklist)}\n"
          f"  Supplier phase: COMPLETE (phase authority)"
      )

  else:  # supplier phase
      # ✅ USER REQUIREMENT: Skip cached + linking map products
      resume_start_index = cached_count + skip_count + 1
      worklist_type = "full_extraction"
      worklist = needs_full_extraction_urls

      self.log.info(
          f"🎯 RESUMING IN SUPPLIER PHASE:\n"
          f"  Resume from product: {resume_start_index}\n"
          f"  Skipping:\n"
          f"    - {skip_count} in linking map (already complete)\n"
          f"    - {cached_count} in cache (already extracted)\n"
          f"  Products to process: {len(worklist)}"
      )

  # ✅ COMPREHENSIVE RESUME EVIDENCE LOG
  self.log.info(
      f"📋 FILE-BASED RESUME CALCULATION:\n"
      f"  Phase (AUTHORITY): {persisted_phase}\n"
      f"  Category: {category_url_normalized}\n"
      f"  Resume from product: {resume_start_index}\n"
      f"  Denominator: {in_count}\n"
      f"  Evidence:\n"
      f"    - Total URLs extracted: {in_count}\n"
      f"    - Linking map (skip): {skip_count}\n"
      f"    - Supplier cache: {cached_count}\n"

... in passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py, line ~5215:

Likely cause
Inside _extract_supplier_products(...) we reference normalize_url in a dict-comprehension but something in that function makes normalize_url local (e.g., an in-function import or assignment), so Python treats it as a local that hasn’t been bound yet at the point of use. AND 

  Consolidated Audit Report: Root Cause Analysis of Resumption Failure

  Objective: This report provides a definitive analysis of why the system's startup and resumption capabilities are failing. It synthesizes findings from multiple audits and justifies
  every conclusion with evidence from scripts, log files, and JSON output files, providing surgical diffs for the required fixes.

  Executive Summary: The Core Problem

  The resumption process is failing due to a single, critical flaw in the startup logic of the main workflow script (tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py).

  On startup, the workflow incorrectly detects a "reverse gap" (where the linking map has more products than the supplier cache). This triggers a faulty logic path that incorrectly resets
  the entire processing state, wiping out all previous progress and forcing the run to start from the beginning.

  All other observed issues—such as the phase resetting to "supplier", the category index resetting to 1, and the EAN/file-based filters appearing to fail—are symptoms of this primary
  state-reset bug. The logic for those features is largely in place, but it is being fed incorrect data from a state that has been wrongly wiped clean.

  The fixes detailed below focus on correcting this faulty startup logic and addressing other latent bugs that contribute to system instability.

  ---

  Part 1: Critical Findings & Agreed-Upon Issues

  This section details the most critical bugs, including those identified by both analyses.

  Finding #1: (CRITICAL) State is Incorrectly Reset on Resumption

   * Issue Identified: The system fails to resume, instead starting a fresh run and overwriting existing progress.
   * Root Cause: The workflow script, not the state manager, contains flawed logic. In passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py, the phase detection logic incorrectly identifies a "reverse gap"
     (linking_map_count > supplier_cache_count) and decides this requires a full reset via the "reverse_gap_cache_rebuild" code path. This is the central bug that causes the entire resumption
      to fail.
   * Evidence:
       1. Log File (fba_extraction_20251007.log): The log explicitly shows the faulty decision being made at startup.

   1         INFO - 🔄 REVERSE GAP DETECTED: Linking map (10419) > Cache (10258)
   2         INFO - ✅ REVERSE GAP: Reset resumption_index = 0 (explicit cache rebuild requested)
   3         INFO - RESUME DECISION: START_AT_INDEX=0 (reason: reverse_gap_cache_rebuild)
       2. State File (..._processing_state.json): The state file confirms this decision was persisted, showing a reset index despite evidence of prior work.

   1         {
   2           "resume_reason": "reverse_gap_cache_rebuild",
   3           "resumption_index": 0,
   4           "system_progression": {
   5             "resumption_ptr": { "cat_idx": 161, "prod_idx": 0 }
   6           }
   7         }
       3. Script File (utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py): The perform_startup_analysis method contains the logic that, when triggered by the workflow, resets the index.

   1         # This block is incorrectly triggered by the workflow
   2         elif file_grounded_data["linking_map_count"] > file_grounded_data["total_products"]:
   3             log.info(f"🔄 REVERSE GAP DETECTED: ...")
   4             if explicit_cache_rebuild: // This is being set to True incorrectly
   5                 self.state_data["resumption_index"] = 0 // This is the reset
   * Suggested Fix: The most surgical fix is to prevent the "reverse gap" logic from catastrophically resetting the resumption_index. The explicit_cache_rebuild flag should not be triggered
     by a simple count mismatch. The logic should be adjusted to preserve the index.

   * Diff for utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py:

    1     --- a/utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py
    2     +++ b/utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py
    3     @@ -603,12 +603,13 @@

    5              explicit_cache_rebuild = self.state_data.get("force_cache_rebuild", False)
    6
    7 -            if explicit_cache_rebuild:
    8 -                # Only reset to 0 if explicitly rebuilding cache
    9 -                self.state_data["resumption_index"] = 0
   10 -                self.state_data["resume_reason"] = "reverse_gap_cache_rebuild"
   11 -                log.info(
   12 -                    f"✅ REVERSE GAP: Reset resumption_index = 0 (explicit cache rebuild requested)"
   13 -                )
   14 -            elif current_resumption_index == 0:
   15 +            # DO NOT reset to 0 on reverse gap unless it's a true fresh start.
   16 +            # Preserve the existing index to allow processing to continue.

   18 +                log.warning(
   19 +                    f"🔄 REVERSE GAP: Preserving existing resumption_index = {current_resumption_index} (no explicit rebuild)"
   20 +                )
   21 +                self.state_data["resume_reason"] = "reverse_gap_preserved_resume"
   22 +            elif current_resumption_index == 0:
   23                  # If resumption_index is 0, check if this is truly a fresh start or a restart
   24                  # 🚨 FIX 1: Use enhanced fresh start detection instead of manual logic
   25                  is_actual_fresh_start = self._detect_actual_fresh_start()

  Finding #2: Latent UnboundLocalError Crash Risk

   * Issue Identified: The application is at risk of crashing due to an UnboundLocalError related to the normalize_url function.
   * Root Cause: As your report correctly identified, this is due to function-scoped imports. Importing normalize_url inside a function causes Python to treat it as a local variable for the
     entire function scope. If it's used in a comprehension before the import statement is reached, the program crashes.
   * Evidence:
       1. Script File (utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py): The faulty pattern exists in multiple functions.

   1         def update_discovered_products_in_category(...):
   2             from utils.normalization import normalize_url # Local import
   3
   4         def initialize_category_processing(...):
   5             from utils.normalization import normalize_url # Local import
   * Suggested Fix: Remove all function-scoped imports of normalize_url and rely on the single, existing module-level import.
   * Diff for utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py:

    1     --- a/utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py

6) normalize_url UnboundLocalError risk
Your runtime logs showed this crash earlier.

Report A: flags function-scope imports remain; recommends removing them.

Report B: same idea.

My verification: ✅ This risk still exists in both files:

State manager still has multiple function-scope imports of normalize_url (e.g., at ~658, ~2634), in addition to the module-level import at ~53.

Workflow also has function-scope imports of normalize_url (e.g., ~7541), even though there’s a module-level import at ~106.

If any function uses normalize_url before the inner from utils.normalization import normalize_url executes, Python treats it as a local var and raises UnboundLocalError.

Verdict: Must remove all function-scope normalize_url imports across both files and rely solely on the top-level import.

Objective: Make resumption correct and stable by (1) respecting persisted phase and category index at startup, (2) using EAN-first skipping, (3) computing denominators & resume starts from file-based filter results, (4) removing local imports, (5) adding observability.

    sp["persistent_category_index"] = int(category_index)

    incoming, current = int(category_index), int(current_pci)
    if incoming < current:
        sp["persistent_category_index"] = current  # ✅ explicit preservation

3) Workflow: EAN-first linking-map filter (Fix #2)

Change to EAN-first with URL fallback and clear logs:

skip_entirely_urls = []
remaining_after_linking_map = []

for url in urls_for_manifest:
    normalized_url = normalize_url(url)

    # Look up EAN from cache by normalized URL
    product_ean = None
    if hasattr(self, "product_cache_url_index"):
        p = self.product_cache_url_index.get(normalized_url)
        if p:
            product_ean = p.get("ean")

    skip_due_to_linking_map = False

    # PRIMARY: EAN-based skip
    if product_ean and product_ean in processed_eans:
        skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
        skip_due_to_linking_map = True
        self.log.debug("🔗 EAN-based linking map skip: %s (EAN: %s)", url, product_ean)

    # SECONDARY: URL-based skip
    elif normalized_url in processed_urls:
        skip_entirely_urls.append(url)
        skip_due_to_linking_map = True
        self.log.debug("🔗 URL-based linking map skip: %s", url)

    if not skip_due_to_linking_map:
        remaining_after_linking_map.append(url)

self.log.info("📊 LINKING MAP FILTER RESULTS: total=%d skip=%d remaining=%d",
              len(urls_for_manifest), len(skip_entirely_urls), len(remaining_after_linking_map))
4) Workflow: File-based denominators + resume start calculation (Fix #3)
Add right after the two-step filter completes. Use the filter outputs to set denominators and compute the resume starting index, respecting the persisted phase:

sp = self.state_manager.state_data.get("system_progression", {})
persisted_phase = sp.get("current_phase", "supplier")

in_count   = len(urls_for_manifest)          # total extracted URLs for the category
skip_count = len(skip_entirely_urls)         # in linking map
cached_count = len(needs_amazon_only_urls)   # already cached on supplier side
full_count = len(needs_full_extraction_urls) # needs supplier+amazon

# Invariant
if in_count != skip_count + cached_count + full_count:
    self.log.error("🚨 FILTER INVARIANT VIOLATION: in=%d skip=%d cached=%d full=%d",
                   in_count, skip_count, cached_count, full_count)
else:
    self.log.info("✅ FILTER INVARIANT VALIDATED: in=%d == skip=%d + cached=%d + full=%d",
                  in_count, skip_count, cached_count, full_count)

# Denominators (both phases equal to extracted URL count)
sp["supplier_products_needing_extraction"] = in_count
sp["amazon_products_needing_analysis"] = in_count

# Resume start (phase-aware)
if persisted_phase == "amazon_analysis":
    resume_start_index = skip_count + 1               # after linking map
    worklist = needs_amazon_only_urls
    self.log.info("🎯 RESUMING IN AMAZON PHASE: start=%d after skip=%d items", resume_start_index, skip_count)
else:
    resume_start_index = cached_count + skip_count + 1  # skip cached + linking map
    worklist = needs_full_extraction_urls
    self.log.info("🎯 RESUMING IN SUPPLIER PHASE: start=%d (skip cached=%d + link=%d)",
                  resume_start_index, cached_count, skip_count)

self.log.info("📋 FILE-BASED RESUME CALCULATION: phase=%s denom=%d",
              persisted_phase, in_count)
This satisfies your requirement: both denominators equal extracted URLs per category; no “frozen” denominator is required for control, though you may store a frozen copy for validation only.

What will change in behavior (and why it fixes your symptoms)
No more phase/index resets on startup: The workflow stops forcing supplier before evidence exists, and the state manager stops overwriting current_phase while explicitly preserving PCI on backslides.

EAN-first prevents reprocessing products that share an EAN but have different URLs (your exact requirement).

Resume pointers are computed only from file-based counts (linking map + cache + full-extraction lists), not from volatile session counters.

Both denominators (supplier_products_needing_extraction, amazon_products_needing_analysis) come from the extracted URL count for the category, exactly as you specified (no dependency on “freeze” to drive behavior).

Observability: LOADED vs RESUME logs + FILE-BASED evidence logs will clearly prove what the system loaded and how it decided, every run.

Here’s the blunt verdict up front: **Report #2 (“Consolidated Audit…”) is closer to the truth about the root cause**, but **Report #1 (“Comprehensive Audit…”) correctly identifies the *timing* bug (premature gating/phase switch) and several accurate mitigations**. The real picture is the combination of both: the workflow’s *reverse-gap* detection path is being treated as a **fresh-start** and is **executed too early**, so it **overrides** the state manager’s correct, file-grounded resumption. # Detailed comparison (agree / partial / disagree)

## Where I **agree** (or mostly agree)

1. **State manager is largely correct and phase/index shouldn’t be clobbered.**
   Your state manager computes a proper resume index (10786) from file-grounded data, and it preserves phase/PCI. This is recorded twice during startup:

> “**RESUME DECISION: START_AT_INDEX=10786 (reason: system_progression)**”  
> “**Loaded state for poundwholesale.co.uk – resumption from index 10786**”  

2. **Premature gating / phase switch in the workflow is the practical failure mode.**
   Immediately after the state manager gives a correct answer, the workflow performs its own phase detection and logs **FRESH_CATEGORIES (reverse gap)**, then proceeds as a **fresh start** with index reset:

> “**[PHASE_COUNTS] … lm_count=10786 … cache_count=10232**”  
> “**PHASE DETECTION: FRESH_CATEGORIES (reverse gap – linking map: 10786 > cache: 10232)**”  
> “**🆕 FRESH START: Phase switched to supplier with index reset**”  

3. **Function-scope normalize_url imports are risky (latent UnboundLocalError).**
   I can’t see the source file here, but the pattern is indeed dangerous in Python. Report #1’s remediation (remove function-scope imports; keep module-level import) is sound. (No contradiction with logs.)

4. **EAN-first linking-map filter exists and is fine; not the root cause.**
   The logs show robust indexing and hashing of EAN/URL/ASIN with O(1) lookups:

> “**HASH INDEX BUILT: 10310 EANs, 10702 URLs, 6768 ASINs**” (twice, for two loads)  
> So the resume failure isn’t from missing EAN logic; it’s from startup routing.

## Where I **partially agree**

1. **Report #2’s root cause (“reverse gap” triggers reset) is right, but the *reset is happening in the workflow*, not in the state manager.**
   *Three sources of truth (log snippets):*

* State manager **chooses** index 10786 (resume):  
* Workflow **declares reverse gap** and fresh-category policy:  
* Workflow **forces fresh-start index reset**:

   Your logs show the opposite: the state manager chooses **10786**, while the **workflow** does the fresh-start reset.

# Master Implementation Plan (no assumptions; all changes are surgical and anchored to what we can see)

## P0 — Fix the root cause (prevent fresh-start from overriding a valid resume)

**Goal:** If file-grounded evidence (linking-map count, cache count, frozen denominators, persisted phase/PCI) indicates prior progress, the workflow must **never** choose the “fresh-start/index reset” path—even when a reverse gap is detected.

**Change A — Guard the *reverse-gap* decision in the workflow**

**Why:** Logs show the workflow chooses **FRESH_CATEGORIES (reverse gap)** and then logs **“🆕 FRESH START … index reset”**, despite a valid resume index 10786 from the state manager.    

**Patch (grep-anchored hunk, safe on Windows):**

diff
*** tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py (anchor: "PHASE DETECTION: FRESH_CATEGORIES")
@@
- self.log.info("🆕 FRESH START: Phase switched to supplier with index reset")
- self.state_manager.commit_phase_switch(new_phase="supplier", reset_index=True)
+ # Reverse-gap ≠ fresh start if resume evidence exists.
+ sp_loaded = self.state_manager.state_data.get("system_progression", {})
+ resume_idx  = int(self.state_manager.state_data.get("resumption_index", 0))
+ has_frozen  = bool(sp_loaded.get("frozen_category_denominators"))
+ persisted   = bool(sp_loaded.get("current_phase"))
+ if resume_idx > 0 or has_frozen or persisted:
+     self.log.info("✅ GAP-FILL MODE: reverse-gap detected, preserving index/phase (resume_idx=%s)", resume_idx)
+     # Preserve current phase and indices; no reset here.
+     self.state_manager.commit_phase_switch(new_phase="supplier", reset_index=False)
+ else:
+     self.log.info("🆕 FRESH START: Phase switched to supplier with index reset (no resume evidence)")
+     self.state_manager.commit_phase_switch(new_phase="supplier", reset_index=True)


**Acceptance criteria (must pass):**

* After startup you still see
  “**RESUME DECISION: START_AT_INDEX=10786**” (state manager), **and you do NOT see** “🆕 FRESH START … index reset” when resume_idx>0 or frozen denominators/persisted phase exist.
  (Compare to current log lines showing the bad behavior.)  

**Change B — Defer destructive decisions until after totals are frozen**

* Your workflow itself warns: “**Frozen totals NOT committed, resume pointers may be unreliable**” right before it queries for an “authoritative resumption point,” then it routes to supplier anyway.  
* Ensure you **freeze category totals first**, then compute phase/index routing, then proceed.

**Patch (anchor: "Frozen totals NOT committed"):**

diff
*** tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py
@@
- self.log.warning("⚠️ RESUME PROOF: Frozen totals NOT committed, resume pointers may be unreliable")
- self.log.info("Requesting authoritative resumption point from State Manager...")
+ self.log.warning("⚠️ RESUME PROOF: Frozen totals NOT committed → committing now before routing")
+ self.state_manager.commit_frozen_totals_if_needed()  # idempotent helper you already use elsewhere
+ self.log.info("Requesting authoritative resumption point from State Manager (after freeze)...")


**Acceptance criteria:** You should then see
“**🔒 TOTALS COMMITTED: Resume pointers now enabled**” *before* any phase/route decision. (You already emit this later in the run—bring it forward.)

## P1 — Stability hardening (low risk, clear wins)

**Change C — Remove function-scope normalize_url imports**

* Keep the top-level import in utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py. (Matches both reports’ guidance; avoids latent UnboundLocalError.)

**Change D — Windows-safe manifest save (fix the fcntl import error)**

* You hit: “**Failed to save manifest … No module named 'fcntl'**” during manifest write for category 1.  
* Use your already-working **WindowsSaveGuardian** for this path as well, or conditionally import msvcrt on Windows.

Patch (pseudo-hunk; wrap your manifest writer):

diff
*** tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py (anchor: "Failed to save manifest")
@@
- save_manifest_atomic(path, data)  # currently uses fcntl on all OSes
+ try:
+     save_manifest_atomic(path, data)
+ except ImportError as e:
+     if "fcntl" in str(e) and os.name == "nt":
+         self.log.info("🔁 Retrying manifest save via WindowsSaveGuardian (no fcntl on Windows)")
+         windows_save_guardian.save_json_atomic(path, data)
+     else:
+         raise


**Change E — Observability: keep both “LOADED STATE” and “AUTHORITATIVE RESUME” logs**

* They already exist (good!). Keep them as your first lines *after* state load so you always have pre-routing evidence.  

**Change F — Optional: guarded BrowserManager cleanup on shutdown**

* Low-risk and consistent with Report #1’s suggestion (to avoid “event loop closed” on teardown).

* Ensure runtime imports point to **utils/fixed_enhanced_state_manager.py** (not experimental new/ variants).

   * Expect **no** “🆕 FRESH START … index reset” if resumption_index>0 or phase/frozen-denominator evidence exists. Compare to prior bad lines. 
   * Expect:

     * “**RESUME DECISION: START_AT_INDEX=10786**” (state manager) 
     * “**LOADED STATE …**” and “**AUTHORITATIVE RESUME …**” before routing. 

2. **Reverse-gap scenario validation** (linking > cache)

   * Expect the new log: “**✅ GAP-FILL MODE … preserving index/phase**” (instead of fresh-start reset).
   * Category 1 should **start at product 0/58** *without* zeroing global resumption. You already freeze 58 items for that category later:
     “**FROZEN DENOMINATOR: Category … → 58 products (LOCKED)**”  

3. **Windows manifest write**

   * Expect **no** fcntl ImportError and a successful save via WindowsSaveGuardian; prior saves already succeed through it:
     “**ATOMIC SAVE: … saved successfully**” (multiple occurrences)

## Rollback plan

* All changes are additive/guarded. If anything regresses, flip the guard so reverse-gap falls back to *existing* behavior; no data migrations required. Commit each change as a separate PR for easy revert.

Example guard patch (guidance for /sc:plan → /sc:review)
(Do not blindly paste; adjust to your code anchors.)

# In tools/passive_extraction_workflow_latest.py, inside the block that logs:
# "PHASE DETECTION: FRESH_CATEGORIES (reverse gap ...)"

sp = self.state_manager.state_data.get("system_progression", {})
resume_idx = int(self.state_manager.state_data.get("resumption_index", 0))
has_frozen = bool(sp.get("frozen_category_denominators"))
has_phase  = bool(sp.get("current_phase"))

if resume_idx > 0 or has_frozen or has_phase:
    self.log.info("✅ GAP-FILL MODE: reverse-gap detected, preserving index/phase (resume_idx=%s)", resume_idx)
    self.state_manager.commit_phase_switch(new_phase="supplier", reset_index=False)
else:
    self.log.info("🆕 FRESH START: Phase switched to supplier with index reset (no resume evidence)")
    self.state_manager.commit_phase_switch(new_phase="supplier", reset_index=True)
Why this is safe: it never removes your late, file-based resume logic (which is correct), it just prevents the early override. And the state manager already preserves PCI/phase and supports gap-fill resumption.

Known false leads to ignore
“EAN-first filter missing” — it exists; the resume failure predates its output. Keep it. (The late resume calc already relies on counts it produces.)

“State manager resets index on reverse gap” — current code preserves when not truly fresh.

Success criteria (must all be true)
No “🆕 FRESH START … index reset” when prior progress exists in state/logs. (The bad lines disappear.)

LOADED → AUTHORITATIVE → FILE-BASED CALC → RESUME routing sequence is visible and consistent.

Supplier resume index = cached + skip + 1; Amazon resume index = skip + 1.

Phase & PCI match previous run; category does not snap back to 1 on restart.

(Optional) Teardown nicety
If you still see intermittent teardown warnings, wrap optional browser cleanup with a getattr(..., "cleanup", None) guard and ignore “event loop is closed” in RuntimeError.

That’s it. Run the command sequence above, keep these guardrails pinned via /sc:instructions, and apply the one guarded change to the early gate. Everything else in your late resume calc + state manager should then work as intended.
